  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5b5e8226-6401-409b-b3c0-8f02dd339c98'
      });

But when her mother dies under mysterious circumstances, she is summoned to the majestic city of Sky. There, to her shock, Yeine is named an heiress to the king. <a href="/questions/540712-is-the-whole-series-connected-in-one-way">Is the whole series connected in one way or another or is it a separate book series?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_540712'><a id="like_count_community_question_540712" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/540712?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">3 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F6437061-the-hundred-thousand-kingdoms">like</a></span>

</li>

<a href="/questions/540712-is-the-whole-series-connected-in-one-way">Add your answer</a>
</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/10341771-cameron"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/10341771-cameron">Cameron</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">All 3 books in the trilogy take place in the same world in chronological order, so reading them out of order causes major spoilers for the previous bo<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">All 3 books in the trilogy take place in the same world in chronological order, so reading them out of order causes major spoilers for the previous books. There are overlapping characters and plot points, and actions in one book have consequences in the next. For the most part there is not a continuous plot between the books, but you could argue that there is a continuous narrative surrounding how the fictional world changes over time due to the combined events of the books.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerFooter'>

<div id="review_1372922646" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1372922646" />
    <a title="Rick Riordan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan"><img alt="Rick Riordan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442449448p2/25375513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1372922646?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rick Riordan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rick Riordan" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan">Rick Riordan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1372922646" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5818308012788633119">I picked up this book after reading a thought-provoking article about the author in The Guardian: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.theguardian.com/books/2015/jul/27/nk-jemisin-interview-fantasy-science-fiction-writing-racism-sexism'>http://www.theguardian.com/books/2015...</a>. I really liked what she said about coming to fantasy with no interest in maintaining the status quo. She's right that so many fantasy books are about restoring order to a kingdom, returning a rightful heir to the throne, or getting back to the good old days by defeating some dark power that threatens to unbalance society. Jemisin, as an African American fema</span>
  <span id="freeText5818308012788633119" style="display:none">I picked up this book after reading a thought-provoking article about the author in The Guardian: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.theguardian.com/books/2015/jul/27/nk-jemisin-interview-fantasy-science-fiction-writing-racism-sexism">http://www.theguardian.com/books/2015...</a>. I really liked what she said about coming to fantasy with no interest in maintaining the status quo. She's right that so many fantasy books are about restoring order to a kingdom, returning a rightful heir to the throne, or getting back to the good old days by defeating some dark power that threatens to unbalance society. Jemisin, as an African American female writer, says this simply doesn't resonate with her or interest her, and why should it? Instead, she writes science fiction which challenges those in power, threatens the ordered society, and questions whether the good old days ever existed. I like books that force me to rethink paradigms, so I decided to check out her work.<br /><br />The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms is a wonderful read. The first book of a trilogy, it introduces us to Yeine Darr, an outcast from the ruling family of Sky and the product of an unsanctioned biracial marriage, who is summoned home to the palace and suddenly made one of three heirs to the throne for reasons unclear. Soon she is locked in a cold war with her two cousins, both of whom have much more power and understanding of politics. But Yeine gains some powerful if unstable allies: the Enefadah, gods who were enslaved by the ruling family after those deities lost a war against the Lord of Light, the patron god of Sky.<br /><br />You know me. I can't resist a good book with gods knocking around, causing chaos among mortals. I loved the mythology Jemisin created, and how she turned the bright shiny castle with the glorious white king and the heavenly patron god into just about the most horrible place you can image. I'm looking forward to the next two books, though after that ending (NO SPOILERS, BUT WOW) I have no idea where she will go with the story!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5818308012788633119" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/149352316" />
    <a title="Vinaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya"><img alt="Vinaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294127450p2/4687823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/149352316?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vinaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vinaya" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya">Vinaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781841498171" href="/book/show/6612542-the-hundred-thousand-kingdoms">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=mixed-vibes">mixed-vibes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=not-for-me">not-for-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=books-i-ought-to-love-but-dont">books-i-ought-to-love-but-dont</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=could-have-been-better">could-have-been-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer149352316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4751508858405329932">I think I may have read too much fantasy. <br/><br/>I'm always apprehensive when I read a book everyone loved and can't get worked up about it. I was expecting this book to be radical and innovative and unusual. It wasn't.<br/><br/>You've read this before.<br/>You're too harsh.<br/>This writing style-<br/> <br/> **********<br/><br/>Makes no narrative sense. <br/><br/>Seriously, what is it about this book I'm missing? What makes it worthy of being a Hugo and Nebula nominee? The choppy writing style felt weird to me- not because I didn't understand the tra</span>
  <span id="freeText4751508858405329932" style="display:none">I think I may have read too much fantasy. <br /><br />I'm always apprehensive when I read a book everyone loved and can't get worked up about it. I was expecting this book to be radical and innovative and unusual. It wasn't.<br /><br />You've read this before.<br />You're too harsh.<br />This writing style-<br /> <br /> **********<br /><br />Makes no narrative sense. <br /><br />Seriously, what is it about this book I'm missing? What makes it worthy of being a Hugo and Nebula nominee? The choppy writing style felt weird to me- not because I didn't understand the transitions in time, but because there was no <i>need</i> for it. It felt more gimmicky than real. <br /><br />The plot line was standard, standard, standard. Orphaned warrior girl is thrust into the midst of a political war and named heir to her grandfather's kingdom, whereupon she falls in love with a god and finds out deep, dark secrets about herself. <br /><br />You want to know who wrote this plotline better? <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15890.Trudi_Canavan" title="Trudi Canavan" rel="nofollow noopener">Trudi Canavan</a>, that's who. Her <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28248.Priestess_of_the_White__Age_of_the_Five___1_" title="Priestess of the White (Age of the Five, #1) by Trudi Canavan" rel="nofollow noopener">Priestess of the White</a> and the following books in the Age of the Five trilogy are teeming with gods and goddesses and deceit and political intrigue and romance and war and betrayal and <b>life</b>. The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms is a pale approximation of Canavan's vivid worldbuilding. Seriously, Australian authors kick ass, every time. <br /><br />The worldbuilding in this book was lacklustre. So many things were never explained; so many rules were pointless and unworkable. I never felt a strong connection with Yeine- so much of her time was spent wandering around aimlessly and hoping to bump into someone who would drop the information onto her lap. All the things we were <i>told</i> in the beginning- that she was a warrior, that she was the competent ruler of an entire nation, that she was trained by her mother in Amn ways... none of these things are actually reflected in her actions. <br /><br />And my other big pet peeve was with the whole sex scene. Seriously, all I got were weird allusions that weren't remotely moving or sexy. Mostly, I was going, WTF?!!! If sex with Nahadoth hadn't been built up to be such a big deal, I could have dealt with the way it was handled; as things stand, though, the description of the scene was florid and overblown and unconvincing. <br /><br />Don't get me wrong, I didn't HATE the book. It was interesting enough to have me reading till the end, but I <i>know</i> what good fantasy reads like, and to me, this book comes a poor second to the vibrant writing of authors like Trudi Canavan and Jennifer Fallon and even Melina Marchetta. Hmmm... they're all Australian, too! </span>
  <a data-text-id="4751508858405329932" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_218417507" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/218417507" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/218417507?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=awards">awards</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=female-lead">female-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=multi-culti">multi-culti</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer218417507" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11235036785323018631">I've just realized I'm about to give two entirely different books the exact same rating for entirely different reasons. Somehow, that is profoundly unsatisfying to my bookish need to categorize. I need a GR ratings intervention.<br/><br/>Something about "The Hundred" fails to digest well. Falling back on my inevitable food analogies, it felt like all those ingredients I love were there--sugar, flour, butter, vanilla, chocolate--but scrambled, fried and decorated into a concoction I wanted to love but just</span>
  <span id="freeText11235036785323018631" style="display:none">I've just realized I'm about to give two entirely different books the exact same rating for entirely different reasons. Somehow, that is profoundly unsatisfying to my bookish need to categorize. I need a GR ratings intervention.<br /><br />Something about "The Hundred" fails to digest well. Falling back on my inevitable food analogies, it felt like all those ingredients I love were there--sugar, flour, butter, vanilla, chocolate--but scrambled, fried and decorated into a concoction I wanted to love but just couldn't.<br /><br />The positives: First and foremost, themes dealt with issues of slavery, servitude, class status and divinity in a very unusual but thoughtful way. It avoided preaching, instead showing how even powerful personalities devolved and struggled under subjugation. Two, information sharing was done tolerably well and did not suffer from the common fantasy 'info-dump' syndrome. As Yeine, the narrator, is new to the city of Sky and her Arameri relatives, the process of orienting her orients the reader. Three, the author also makes a point of giving characters unconventional, multi-ethnic looks and backgrounds, including a female lead who is "short, brown and flat, with unruly curly hair." It's always a positive to see something beyond the tall/leggy or curvaceous stereotypes, and to see women capable of playing multiple roles within a book that are not dependent on sexuality. Lastly, at times Jemisin's language impressed me: "This was the sort of thing that made people hate the Arameri--truly hate them, not just resent their power or their willingness to use it. They found so many ways to lie about the things they did. It mocked the suffering of their victims."<br /> <br />Where Jemisin failed to turn the ingredients into deliciousness: First, it felt 'young adult' in tone; though the narrator was supposed to be 19 and heir/ruler to her tribes' lands, she acts and responds in surprisingly naive and young ways at times. She loses her temper with people she's just met. She's preoccupied with finding out what her mother was "really" like. (By the time we are three-fourths through the book, I started to flash on the children's book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/197084.Are_You_My_Mother_" title="Are You My Mother? by P.D. Eastman" rel="nofollow noopener">Are You My Mother?</a>). She's uncomfortable with sex and refers to a pool being for "...other things." Her youth was unexpected, and perhaps started me off on the wrong foot as I was anticipating a more mature character. Second, while I appreciate the unconventionality of the female lead's looks, one of the males, Nahadoth, is immediately described as "beautiful." Oh, for young-adult romance stereotypes of the plain girl and the hot unattainable male! Of <i>course </i> he chases her with violent intent shortly after meeting, and <i>of course,</i> he kisses her shortly after they confront each other. Dark, misunderstood, and isolated male just needs to be loved to change. <br /><br />That's like burning the dessert right there. <br /><br />Three, there's excessive use of portentous statements. My feeling is that if one has to rely on such statements as "it would occur to me shortly thereafter..." and "later I would understand that..." you are either not doing your job writing, or you are writing one seriously convoluted narrative. Lastly, and this is definitely a style choice, this story felt mythic, as in constructed like Greek myths, with relatively clear plotting with relatively clear motives implemented in an elaborately convoluted way. It was saved from excessive simplicity by the narrative voice shifting between time periods (although we don't know this at the time), oral histories, and dream-states. It lent padding, but not in the right spots. Almost lastly, it also had weird and uncomfortably sexual overtones with Yeine and a demi-god who regularly appeared in child-form and was sexually abused by her family members. Oh, lastly again, and this time I mean it, I really hate paranormal sex scenes, especially the bed-destroying type. <i>(Prolonged eye-roll).</i> Spare me the youthful expectations and descriptions of metaphysical sex that ends the old self and births the new, and destroys the furniture in the process.<br /><br />How to rate, how to rate? Two and a half to three stars on the personal enjoyment scale. Four stars for dealing with slavery, an unusual religious set-up and language use some of the time. Three for a moderately unsurprising ending that wrapped things up well <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ and evil getting it's due  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Two for including an eye-rolling sex scene, the bad-boy lover, and language use the rest of the time.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11235036785323018631" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_171569348" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/171569348" />
    <a title="Felicia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/666892-felicia"><img alt="Felicia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437521850p2/666892.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/171569348?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Felicia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Felicia" href="/user/show/666892-felicia">Felicia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666892-felicia?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666892-felicia?shelf=faves">faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666892-felicia?shelf=vaginal-fantasy">vaginal-fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer171569348" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12512645709526897751">Well, I really loved this book. Not since I've read Jaqueline Carey's Kushiel series have I been as enamored, in fact they are very evocative of each other, these series.<br/><br/>I had no expectations of this book, in fact I've had an ARC copy by my bed for like a year and a half, and for some reason couldn't get myself to pick it up. I think the cover implies a more epic fantasy feel than it is, really it would appeal to most female-driven urban fantasy fans, but again, i guess it's smart not to slap a </span>
  <span id="freeText12512645709526897751" style="display:none">Well, I really loved this book. Not since I've read Jaqueline Carey's Kushiel series have I been as enamored, in fact they are very evocative of each other, these series.<br /><br />I had no expectations of this book, in fact I've had an ARC copy by my bed for like a year and a half, and for some reason couldn't get myself to pick it up. I think the cover implies a more epic fantasy feel than it is, really it would appeal to most female-driven urban fantasy fans, but again, i guess it's smart not to slap a pretty girl on the cover and restrict yourself to just a female audience. Everyone can enjoy this book, the romantic arc is subtle and not cliched-ly prominent.<br /><br />But basically, this is a lovely fantasy with a strong female protagonist. Yes, she doesn't remain assertive and plot-driving as she should, and really that should have taken a star off, but the contemplative nature of the world-building, and layered motivations and mysteries involving the ensemble overcame that for me. I really felt like it was smart and avoided cliches. And I was totally hooked when the ending paid off SO WELL!<br /><br />Other series this is similar to are Sharon Shinn's Archangel series and Garth Nix's Sabriel. <br /><br />Highly recommended!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12512645709526897751" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_156284690" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/156284690" />
    <a title="mark monday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday"><img alt="mark monday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572672245p2/131922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/156284690?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mark monday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mark monday" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday">mark monday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=fantasy-modern">fantasy-modern</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156284690" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6508956910609027596">a pleasingly old-fashioned fantasy - and by <i>old-fashioned</i>, i mean the opposite of the dense, complicated, multiple perspective, incredibly epic mega-fantasies that have had the most popularity over the past couple decades. this is something different. the language is straightforward, for the most part, and certainly beautiful at times. although the mystery is a complicated one, and deals with rather large issues such as the making and unmaking of an entire world, it still feels somehow 'miniatur</span>
  <span id="freeText6508956910609027596" style="display:none">a pleasingly old-fashioned fantasy - and by <i>old-fashioned</i>, i mean the opposite of the dense, complicated, multiple perspective, incredibly epic mega-fantasies that have had the most popularity over the past couple decades. this is something different. the language is straightforward, for the most part, and certainly beautiful at times. although the mystery is a complicated one, and deals with rather large issues such as the making and unmaking of an entire world, it still feels somehow 'miniature'. for the most part it takes place within one setting: the fabulous floating city of Sky. it also deals with gods who are enslaved to mortals. and yet there is an almost underpopulated feeling to it - we get to know only a handful of Sky's denizens and only a handful of gods are introduced. at times, it felt like i was reading an adult fairy tale or a lengthy fable. despite a couple sex scenes, a couple graphic bits of violence, even intimations of rape and molestation, the novel somehow felt... quaint. and this is not a complaint. the novel was refreshing.<br /><br />i really liked the heroine: brave, sardonic, and no-nonsense. i also enjoyed the gods, especially child-god Sieh. loveable and strange little Sieh! a great character. many times when i've read about gods (similar to reading about aliens in scifi), i feel these are actually humans with unusual abilities - they talk and act and respond like humans. not so with Sieh, nor with the other gods. that is a true accomplishment. <br /><br />the mythology was complex in a way, but as with the best myths, there was also a simplicity there. the mythology was genuinely mythic, a far cry from the dungeons &amp; dragons style of mythology that i've seen in many other novels. not many stereotypically human motivations appear when the actions of the various gods are described.<br /><br />overall it felt dreamy and arty and, somehow, minor note... and yet it is the first part of a trilogy describing the beginning and the ending and the renewal of all things. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6508956910609027596" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_156284690'><a id="like_count_review_156284690" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/156284690?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">100 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F6437061-the-hundred-thousand-kingdoms">Like</a></span>

<div id="review_570730503" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/570730503" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/570730503?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=cthulhu-goes-ph-nglui-mglw-nafh-ct">cthulhu-goes-ph-nglui-mglw-nafh-ct</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=reality-bending">reality-bending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fanboy-goes-squee">fanboy-goes-squee</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=worldbuilding-sf">worldbuilding-sf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer570730503" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11927944320780598964">I am and always will be a huge fan of Godpunk fiction.<br/><br/>There's a bit of it floating around out there, but most of it is hidden behind the cloudy minds and bodies of mere mortals, only occasionally poking its bright sunny head out to dazzle and amaze.<br/><br/>Sometimes it's the sun. Sometimes it's not. At the moment, I'm feeling the blaze.<br/><br/>Fortunately for us, we've also got authors with great and deep understanding of the greater and lesser mysteries, the writing chops to pull off an entirely new mythos tha</span>
  <span id="freeText11927944320780598964" style="display:none">I am and always will be a huge fan of Godpunk fiction.<br /><br />There's a bit of it floating around out there, but most of it is hidden behind the cloudy minds and bodies of mere mortals, only occasionally poking its bright sunny head out to dazzle and amaze.<br /><br />Sometimes it's the sun. Sometimes it's not. At the moment, I'm feeling the blaze.<br /><br />Fortunately for us, we've also got authors with great and deep understanding of the greater and lesser mysteries, the writing chops to pull off an entirely new mythos that can turn those mysteries into something brand new again, even if they've been so very, very old. Jemisin has taken us right back to our very beginnings, with the worship of the sun and the void and the great life goddess and given us a truly fantastic tale of revenge, freedom, and most importantly, of love.<br /><br />I sit in awe. I've been fortunate to read a number of really fantastic novels recently, and this one stands tall and proud among them, like a worldtree within a shining forest of worlds.<br /><br />The opening of the novel was unfortunately the weakest part for me, but I was able to feel our heroine's hopeless plight pretty much right away, enjoying her progression of defiance to acceptance as it all became so clear that her life was forfeit no matter what happened. Did I say enjoy? Actually, that part made me squirm quite a bit, but the fact that she was able to come to grips, retain her sanity, and even lose a little more of it in the process, was, in fact, truly enjoyable. I can't believe how tight the romance was, or how cleverly it managed to pull on my heartstrings. (I'm generally not that susceptible to romance on the page. So much of it is unbelievable crap.) In this case, I sank right into it and rooted for them both with all my heart. <br /><br />After finishing the novel, I can't quite see where else it might go except far away from the characters I've just enjoyed, but I've got the entire omnibus sitting right here. I was very satisfied by the end and truly floored by it. I almost want to leave it be and enjoy everything that this novel will eventually become to me.<br /><br />Can anything truly top this ride? </span>
  <a data-text-id="11927944320780598964" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1600043509" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1600043509" />
    <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries"><img alt="Mayim de Vries" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560508357p2/50424456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1600043509?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mayim de Vries" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries">Mayim de Vries</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1600043509" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12027335007476991954"><b>If this is meant to be your first Jemisin book, go away.</b> No, seriously, off you go. Read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1579745844' rel='nofollow noopener'>her masterpiece</a> and only then come back for more. I am writing this thinking that should The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms happened to be my first encounter with Jemisin's writing, it would have taken a long time to approach her again (if at all). But the reversed order allowed me to see how much she matured and developed as a writer and I admire her for this even more.<br/><br/>The plot is simple: a young woman is summon</span>
  <span id="freeText12027335007476991954" style="display:none"><b>If this is meant to be your first Jemisin book, go away.</b> No, seriously, off you go. Read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1579745844" rel="nofollow noopener">her masterpiece</a> and only then come back for more. I am writing this thinking that should The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms happened to be my first encounter with Jemisin's writing, it would have taken a long time to approach her again (if at all). But the reversed order allowed me to see how much she matured and developed as a writer and I admire her for this even more.<br /><br />The plot is simple: a young woman is summoned to be officially recognised as an heir to her Grandfather, a de facto ruler of the world, who had previously disowned her mother due to a mesalliance. When she comes to the seat of power called Sky, she discovers not only the truth behind her mother's murder but also the fact that she is a pawn in a more sinister game between the people and the gods. <br /><br /><b>The plot shows Jemisin "obsession themes", themes that she mastered in Broken Earth but only started playing within the Inheritance series. Admittedly, at times the book is a very clumsy playground.</b> <br /><br /><b> First is her obsession with systems of power.</b> The kingdoms are governed by something that could be called an authoritarian monarchy or perhaps a monarchist theocracy; the power is in the hands of one family called Arameri, and the status of each person within the family depends on blood (full, half, quarter and so on). Needless to say, <b>Jemisin is a staunch believer that power corrupts and absolute power corrupts absolutely and vividly describes it in the book.</b> We have exploitation, corruption, injustice, and institutionalised suffering including slavery, murders, pedophilia, and cannibalism performed in the full blare of authority. Welcome to the underbelly of humanity. On the other edge of the spectrum, there is a just matriarchy of the protagonist's indigenous nation, but I really had to laugh at the naivety and purely utopian quality of certain socio-political concepts (e.g. female superiority in the military). Truly, biology wins over ideology also in a fantasy setting. <br /><br />Secondly, <b>the theme of race permeates Jemisin's writing</b>. On the surface, it is not surprising given that the world is called the Hundred Thousand Kingdoms. But even then it is a bit too much for my tastes. <b>Characters are constantly described and referred to via racial identity markers.</b> Imagine something like: "Asian eyes shone brightly in her pale Caucasian face although the unruly mess of her curls whispered of African ancestry. Only her smile remained Nordic in its coldness." Imagine something like that every second paragraph. I found this style tiring and I think I would find it unacceptable in contemporary fiction. <br /><br />Thirdly, Jemisin's writing is very sensuous. She does not shy away from all things body related. There is plenty of sexual references in her prose albeit not in a tacky Sarah J. Maas' way. This is fine (even if this pretends to be YA). What really bothers me is the way in which <b>Jemisin explores threesomes. No, not love triangles, i.e. one of the most abused themes in literature, but polyamorous and transgender aspects of sexuality</b>. I considered it ingenious in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19161852.The_Fifth_Season__The_Broken_Earth___1_" title="The Fifth Season (The Broken Earth, #1) by N.K. Jemisin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fifth Season</a> where she truly created something new, instead of regurgitating offshoots of our mundane civilisations and moralities. However, <b>The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms is basically a Greek Parthenon meeting the Christian Trinity with so many plotholes in the size of a maelstrom</b>, that I huffed in exasperation very frequently. <br /><br />Finally, be warned that the plot is slow (Yeine comes to the Sky, wanders around, gallivants with gods, talk to few people, sleeps occasionally and weeps at times, discovers the truth and then proceeds to the grand finale), the narrative confusing and jerky (first person retrospective interspersed with short passages from outside the main current of the story), and the heroine problematic (a special snowflake alert). At least I had problems with warming up for her. Overall, a solid 3 stars, mainly for the rich texture of the world and a captivating intrigue. And also for Sieh.<br /><br />PS And if you liked Sieh, you need to try <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31522139.City_of_Miracles__The_Divine_Cities___3_" title="City of Miracles (The Divine Cities, #3) by Robert Jackson Bennett" rel="nofollow noopener">City of Miracles</a>, a book of superior quality in every aspect imaginable. <br /><br />Also in the series: <br /><br />2. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1600043516?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Broken Kingdoms</a><br />3. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1600043522?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Kingdom of Gods</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12027335007476991954" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_128316382" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/128316382" />
    <a title="Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4473627-rachel"><img alt="Rachel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1288327690p2/4473627.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/128316382?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel" href="/user/show/4473627-rachel">Rachel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4473627-rachel?shelf=fantasy-high">fantasy-high</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128316382" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17458820113087015855">This was a commendable first effort, but I cannot bring myself to rate it any higher. In view of all the positive reviews it has been receiving, I just expected more from this story, but, no, it fell completely short of expectations.<br/><br/>The writing itself is certainly readable, but when it comes to portraying emotional turmoils, the author opts for "Tell, Don't Show" too often, so some scenes are filled with rather cringe-worthy descriptions of how a character "feels". The author might have been goi</span>
  <span id="freeText17458820113087015855" style="display:none">This was a commendable first effort, but I cannot bring myself to rate it any higher. In view of all the positive reviews it has been receiving, I just expected more from this story, but, no, it fell completely short of expectations.<br /><br />The writing itself is certainly readable, but when it comes to portraying emotional turmoils, the author opts for "Tell, Don't Show" too often, so some scenes are filled with rather cringe-worthy descriptions of how a character "feels". The author might have been going for sensual, but because the writing lacks natural lyricism, it ends up seem forced than anything else. The world-building begins somewhat promisingly, but the exploration of that world ends up being more cursory than in-depth. The palace intrigues, also, begin with a promise of complex conflicts, but end up quite shallow, and a lot of the said conflicts are resolved via deus ex machina (literally) than through the strength of the nineteen-year-old protagonist.<br /><br />Not all of these issues are serious flaws (and I suppose things like world-building might occur in later volumes of this trilogy), so I might have enjoyed the story for what it is had the characters been more fully-realized. The protagonist, Yeine, does start off with lots of potential. She comes across as endearing and has strength of conviction and other right elements to become an interesting heroine, but in the end she comes off as a Mary Sue in all the wrong ways, especially when it comes to her romantic entanglements. The secondary characters were also imbued with attention-grabbing and flashy personalities, but none of them came across as truly genuine. I am sure I've read mangas with better character developments - actually, what with the detailed descriptions of characters' physical attributes, I did feel like I was reading manga in parts.<br /><br />It's possible I would have enjoyed the story better without the high expectation, but now that I have finished reading it, I simply cannot agree with all the glowing reviews. For years I've been reading as much as I could in this genre, so I know exactly what I want from a fantasy novel, and this, unfortunately, isn't it. Your mileage may vary, of course.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17458820113087015855" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_98250094" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98250094" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98250094?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=unique-magic">unique-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=fantasy-gods">fantasy-gods</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=2006-2010">2006-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98250094" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3153619210118380105">4.0 to 4.5 stars. I learned something while I was reading this excellent fantasy story by Ms. Jemisin that may seem obvious to most but still has changed my outlook on fantasy stories going forward. You see, I have always been a big fan of interesting world-building, compelling back stories and histories and unique magic systems and fantasy elements. The problem is that as you read more and more fantasy stories you start to recognize variations on all the well trod (and often trampled) ground an</span>
  <span id="freeText3153619210118380105" style="display:none">4.0 to 4.5 stars. I learned something while I was reading this excellent fantasy story by Ms. Jemisin that may seem obvious to most but still has changed my outlook on fantasy stories going forward. You see, I have always been a big fan of interesting world-building, compelling back stories and histories and unique magic systems and fantasy elements. The problem is that as you read more and more fantasy stories you start to recognize variations on all the well trod (and often trampled) ground and so it becomes difficult to find something that appears unique and ground-breaking and thus I have been somewhat selective in the fantasy series I have read and if the world/backstory/fantasy elements don’t have something that really catches my eye, I don’t rush it to the top of my reading list.<br /><br />With that said….here is what this wonderful book made me realize…. turns out I only THOUGHT that cool background elements were THE KEY components that drew me to read fantasy books. It turns out…and here is where everyone can smack me on the back of the head and say DUH!!!... it turns out that compelling characters and evocative writing and dialogue are the ESSENTIAL INGREDIENTS in all of my favorite stories and that the world-building, back stories and fantasy elements are just the SPICE that kick a really good story into the amazing category…BAM!! <br /><br />As I look at some of my all time favorite fantasy stories, most from very recently, they include: The First Law Trilogy by Joe Abercrombie (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/944073.The_Blade_Itself__The_First_Law___1_" title="The Blade Itself (The First Law, #1) by Joe Abercrombie" rel="nofollow noopener">The Blade Itself</a>, etc.), The Gentlemen Bastards series by Scott Lynch (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/127455.The_Lies_of_Locke_Lamora__Gentleman_Bastard___1_" title="The Lies of Locke Lamora (Gentleman Bastard, #1) by Scott Lynch" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lies of Locke Lamora</a>, etc.) The Hari Michelson/Over World series by Matthew Stover (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311864.Heroes_Die__Overworld____1_" title="Heroes Die (Overworld, # 1) by Matthew Stover" rel="nofollow noopener">Heroes Die</a>, etc.), A Song of Ice and Fire by George R.R. Martin (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6421982.A_Game_of_Thrones__A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire___1_" title="A Game of Thrones (A Song of Ice and Fire, #1) by George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">A Game of Thrones</a>, etc.), <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1148721.The_Fionavar_Tapestry" title="The Fionavar Tapestry by Guy Gavriel Kay" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fionavar Tapestry</a> by Guy Gavriel Kay, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4407.American_Gods" title="American Gods by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">American Gods</a> by Neil Gaiman, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/186074.The_Name_of_the_Wind__Kingkiller_Chronicle___1_" title="The Name of the Wind (Kingkiller Chronicle, #1) by Patrick Rothfuss" rel="nofollow noopener">The Name of the Wind</a> by Patrick Rothfuss, and my newest addition, the Troy series by David Gemmell (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/257149.Troy_Lord_of_the_Silver_Bow__Troy___1_" title="Troy Lord of the Silver Bow (Troy, #1) by David Gemmell" rel="nofollow noopener">Troy: Lord of the Silver Bow</a>, etc.). As different as all these stories are, they all have the following in common: (1) unforgettable main and supporting characters that draw you to the story and (2) superb, emotionally evocative writing (some poetic, some gritty, some dark and disturbing, some over the top and larger than life, but all of them MAKE YOU FEEL). <br /><br />Now don’t get me wrong, each of the series I mentioned above do in fact have superb world-building and back stories and that is probably what led to some of my inner confusion regarding what I was looking for in a great fantasy read. But then I had …..an EPHIPHANY. What would happen if STEPHANIE MEYER took over writing the next First Law trilogy from Joe Abercrombie? What if GRRM was unable to finish a Song of Ice and First and TERRY BROOKS was brought in to complete it? Thoughts like these caused me to lose sleep and drink WAY TOO MUCH. It also made me see pretty clearly (through blood shot eyes) that the writing and the character portrayals are what MAKE great fantasy and everything else is just a bonus. Conversely, a clever idea will not save poor writing in the execution of a story. <br /><br />Okay, having gone on enough about everything other then the book I am reviewing. how about I start including it in this discussion. Well, I THOUGHT THIS BOOK WAS TERRIFIC for all of the reasons that I explained above make fantasy great for me (see, there is a method to my madness). N.K. Jemisin writes beautifully and I was drawn to the main character Yeine immediately as she was smart, strong willed and self confident. Here is a summary of the back story (which I would hasten to add was excellent and very well done) and plot.<br /><br />BACK STORY/PLOT SUMMARY: In the beginning were 3 gods (for simplicity you can call them Order, Chaos and Balance). Well, by combining elements of Order and Chaos, Balance created the world as we know it and peopled it was humans as well as lesser gods. Eventually, the siblings squabbled and Order killed Balance and imprisoned Chaos (the how and why, I will leave to you to discover). Anyway, the story opens many years after the “god war” and the City of Sky is home to the Arameri who rule “The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms.” The Arameri were the most devoted servants of the god of Order and so he has given them the power to rule. This power is based on the ability of the Arameri to control and use the imprisoned god of Chaos and the lesser gods to do their bidding. These imprisoned gods (called Enefadah) are fully developed and realized individuals and are the most compelling characters in the story. Well the main character Yeine Darr, whose mother was the chosen successor to rule the Arameri and who instead abdicated and was exiled, is brought back to Sky in order to compete for the role of successor to the current ruler of Arameri (her maternal grandfather) and the intrigue, conspiracies, alliances and betrayals quickly ensue. <br /><br />So, overall, I found this to be a compelling first novel in what looks to be an intriguing new series. In addition, I will always be thankful to this story for being an effective catalyst in helping me see what it is I am truly looking for in a fantasy story. HIGHLY RECOMMENDED!!! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3153619210118380105" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3391152435" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3391152435" />
    <a title="James Tivendale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10282461-james-tivendale"><img alt="James Tivendale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605206526p2/10282461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3391152435?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Tivendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Tivendale" href="/user/show/10282461-james-tivendale">James Tivendale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3391152435" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16316398692244227775">The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms follows Yeine, a nineteen-year-old who, at the novel's beginning, is invited to visit her family seat by her grandfather Dekarta Arameri. The family seat is the city of Sky which is the heart of The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms and includes a beautiful and impressive floating palace. The reason for Yeine's invitation is soon revealed and is a surprise to all in attendance. Dekarta names Yeine as his heir which I imagine would have been an excellent revelation if two of</span>
  <span id="freeText16316398692244227775" style="display:none">The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms follows Yeine, a nineteen-year-old who, at the novel's beginning, is invited to visit her family seat by her grandfather Dekarta Arameri. The family seat is the city of Sky which is the heart of The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms and includes a beautiful and impressive floating palace. The reason for Yeine's invitation is soon revealed and is a surprise to all in attendance. Dekarta names Yeine as his heir which I imagine would have been an excellent revelation if two of her cousins weren't already assigned as heirs. To explain his thinking, Dekarta states the below, which sets up the story nicely as Yeine moves to Sky with her relatives, with its political disharmony, and with its Gods that walk the palace corridors.<br /><br />“It is very simple. I have named three heirs. One of you will actually manage to succeed me. The other two will doubtless kill each other or be killed by the victor. As for which lives, and which die—” He shrugged. “That is for you to decide.”<br /><br />The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms is presented in the first-person perspective and follows events over a couple of weeks after Yeine arrives in Sky. As a new addition, she has to figure out how things work in Sky, try to make friends and allies, whilst also trying to uncover how and why her mother was murdered which happened prior to her arrival. In addition, she has started having frequent strange dreams and visions.<br /><br />My favourite aspect of this story was the Gods and the way they mingle with and converse with the inhabitants of Sky. There are four of these Gods and they are essentially prisoners of a great God War. They could be considered slaves or weapons and have to abide by the demands and requests of the ruling family. Yeine included. The way these Gods are presented is similar to the Gods in Malazan Book of the Fallen. I adore it in stories when the Gods have human qualities and characteristics all whilst being much more powerful, intimidating, mysterious and even mischievous. It's interesting here that the Gods, although still formidable beings, are restrained by mortals. My favourite scenes involved Nahadoth (the Nightlord) and his son Seih. The lore and history surrounding the Gods was a joy to read. This is presented to readers through Yeine discussing what she learnt in history books or from the mouths of the Gods themselves in conversations with her. <br /><br />“We can never be gods, after all--but we can become something less than human with frightening ease.” <br /><br />The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms is an enchanting and majestic fantasy read. The novel is written in an eloquent manner and is engaging in the way that it focuses on Yeine's relationships with her family, the people of Sky, and the Gods. Her cousins make fine characters although I didn't see as much of her drunken cousin Relad as I'd have hoped, but I do have a soft spot for drunks in fiction. With a title as grandiose as The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms, it was surprising that the majority of the events take place in Sky alone and we are witness to little that happens elsewhere. As Sky is the centre and controlling nation of these Kingdoms though, the title does make sense yet I do hope that in the following books of the series we do visit other cities and sections of Jemisin's crafted world. Overall, I had an extremely positive experience with this book, my first time reading Jemisin. The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms was an addictive tale that I devoured within four days and I am definitely planning to continue this series and to check out more of the author's back catalogue.<br /><br />“In a child's eyes, a mother is a goddess. She can be glorious or terrible, benevolent or filled with wrath, but she commands love either way. I am convinced that this is the greatest power in the universe.”</span>
  <a data-text-id="16316398692244227775" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_87851274" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87851274" />
    <a title="Brent Weeks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1741767-brent-weeks"><img alt="Brent Weeks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583875272p2/1741767.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/87851274?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brent Weeks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brent Weeks" href="/user/show/1741767-brent-weeks">Brent Weeks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87851274" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16458976205065435545">[This review is based on an Advanced Reading Copy:]<br/><br/>What if gods were real…and walked among us…enslaved…and were used as weapons…and were really pissed off about it?<br/><br/>N.K. Jemisin is a gifted storyteller and The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms is a satisfying tale built on intriguing ideas. Buy this book if you love the flights of imagination only possible in fantasy. Buy it if you love stories of betrayal, murder, hard truths, and being in way over your head.<br/><br/>The book is written in the first person. To b</span>
  <span id="freeText16458976205065435545" style="display:none">[This review is based on an Advanced Reading Copy:]<br /><br />What if gods were real…and walked among us…enslaved…and were used as weapons…and were really pissed off about it?<br /><br />N.K. Jemisin is a gifted storyteller and The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms is a satisfying tale built on intriguing ideas. Buy this book if you love the flights of imagination only possible in fantasy. Buy it if you love stories of betrayal, murder, hard truths, and being in way over your head.<br /><br />The book is written in the first person. To be blunt, I usually hate this. Here, it works. There are scattered, apparent digressions: snippets of history, backstory. This may bother you. I thought it fit, and the digressions served a purpose. Though the story deals with politics at the highest level, the cast is small. For those who get lost and frustrated in a George R. R. Martin-sized cast, this is a boon. Jemisin's characters are clearly differentiated and easy to remember. Those who love additional complexity may wish the cast were larger and the book longer. This is the first book in a trilogy, so I'm sure we'll get to see more in later books. The world is fascinating, but we spend most of this book inside the central palace of Sky. The visuals are clear and cool.<br /><br />[Full disclosure: I have met Ms. Jemisin once, and she is published by the same company I am. However, neither she nor Orbit asked me to do this review.]<br /><br />N.K. Jemisin is a debut novelist who deserves the chance to write many more novels. But you don't care about that, and you shouldn't. The only question that matters to you is, "Among all my other options, is THIS book worth my money and my time?" Yes, and yes. Emphatically.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16458976205065435545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_151015572" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151015572" />
    <a title="Geoffrey Dow" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1081264-geoffrey-dow"><img alt="Geoffrey Dow" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581981797p2/1081264.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151015572?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Geoffrey Dow" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Geoffrey Dow" href="/user/show/1081264-geoffrey-dow">Geoffrey Dow</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151015572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1678566748084835075"><p></p><blockquote>
<em>For the record, my copy of N.K. Jemisin's </em>The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms<em> came courtesy of a <a href='http://triciasullivan.livejournal.com/105907.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>contest</a> conducted by the writer <a href='http://www.triciasullivan.com/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tricia Sullivan</a>, whose novel, <a href='http://www.triciasullivan.com/maul.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Maul</a>, I read a few years back and which which has since stayed with me far more strongly than most. I wish I could say the same about </em>The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms<em>.</em>
</blockquote><br/><br/><strong>Stormwinds over a cardboard world:</strong><br/><strong>
  <em>Nebula-nominated first novel is epic failure</em>
</strong><br/><br/><img alt='' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380346269i/700705.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I opened N.K. Jemisin's (now <a href='http://www.sfwa.org/2011/02/2010-nebula-nominees/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nebula Award</a> nominated) first novel, <em>The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms</em>, ha</span>
  <span id="freeText1678566748084835075" style="display:none"><p></p><blockquote>
<em>For the record, my copy of N.K. Jemisin's </em>The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms<em> came courtesy of a <a href="http://triciasullivan.livejournal.com/105907.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">contest</a> conducted by the writer <a href="http://www.triciasullivan.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Tricia Sullivan</a>, whose novel, <a href="http://www.triciasullivan.com/maul.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Maul</a>, I read a few years back and which which has since stayed with me far more strongly than most. I wish I could say the same about </em>The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms<em>.</em>
</blockquote><br><br><strong>Stormwinds over a cardboard world:</strong><br><strong>
  <em>Nebula-nominated first novel is epic failure</em>
</strong><br><br><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380346269i/700705.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I opened N.K. Jemisin's (now <a href="http://www.sfwa.org/2011/02/2010-nebula-nominees/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Nebula Award</a> nominated) first novel, <em>The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms</em>, having occasionally read the author's blog and commentary elsewhere on the internet, and was well-aware the book had been getting a lot of <a href="http://nkjemisin.com/reviews/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">positive attention</a> since it was published last year. In other words, I was looking forward to reading at least a very good debut novel and hoping for even more than that.<br><br>Instead, I find myself obliged to discuss a first novel about which I can find almost nothing good to say whatsoever — except to note that, on page 222, the author offers a striking and (I think) original metaphor for the female orgasm.<br><br><em>The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms</em> is a novel remarkable only for the lack of detail and verisimilitude of its world-building, the droning sameness of its characters (god or human — you can't tell them apart), the thoughtlessly anachronistic dialogue and banality of its prose.<br><br><em>The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms</em> is not the worst novel I've ever read (there are lots of bad books out there), but it might be the worst <em>highly-praised</em> science fiction novel I've ever come across (I say "might" because it has been many years since I read <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lord_of_Light" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Lord of Light</em>
</a>).<br><br>The basics include a number of standard fantasy tropes. A world not quite our own, shared by humans and a more ancient and powerful race; a heroine with a Special Destiny; a society with a pre-industrial technology (plus magic) and a feudal political order with a cruel and corrupt extended family at the top of the heap.<br><br>There's nothing inherently wrong with re-using the familiar to tell a story, but there is a lot wrong with using those tropes so badly the reader never feels they are looking in on another world, let alone that they have actually <em>entered</em> into what Tolkien called a <em>secondary creation</em>.<br><br>For a fantasy to succeed, it must convince the reader of not only the reality of its narrative but of that narrative's background. The author must pay attention to such things as his or her world's history and culture, to its tools and technology, as much as to character and psychology.<br><br>To my ears, neither Jemisin's world-building nor her character-building convince, let alone provide cause to care. Worse, her prose is sophomoric and her dialogue painfully melodramatic.<br><br><blockquote>I did not answer, and after a moment Scimina sighed.<br><br>"So," she said, "there are new alliances being formed on Darr's borders, meant to counter Darr's perceived new strength. Since Darr in fact <em>has</em> no new strength, that means the entire region is becoming unstable. Hard to say what will happen under circumstances like that."<br><br>My fingers itched for a sharpened stone. "Is that a threat?"<br><br>"Please, Cousin. I'm merely passing the information along. We Arameri must look out for one another."<br><br>"I appreciate your concern." I turned to leave, before my temper slipped any further ...</blockquote><br><br><a href="http://ed-rex.com/unpopular_arts/books/the_hundred_thousand_kingdoms" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">These are not words that sing, nor dialogue that breathes. Is there <em>anything</em> in this book that does? Click to read more.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1678566748084835075" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1285425123" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1285425123" />
    <a title="Hannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788446-hannah"><img alt="Hannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475256742p2/41788446.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1285425123?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah" href="/user/show/41788446-hannah">Hannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780316043922" href="/book/show/7901864-the-hundred-thousand-kingdoms">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788446-hannah?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788446-hannah?shelf=loved-it">loved-it</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1285425123" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11049870338279970568">Books like this one are the reason why I read and love fantasy. N. K. Jemisin has a way of creating believable and exciting worlds that make me think about my own in a way that I haven't before. While the world in this series is (so far/ for me) not as impressive as the one created in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19161852.The_Fifth_Season__The_Broken_Earth___1_' title='The Fifth Season (The Broken Earth, #1) by N.K. Jemisin' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Fifth Season</a>, it is still highly original and a wonderful basis for the type of stories she excells in.<br/><br/>Set in a world where after a war between the gods some of those gods are enslaved by humans and one is reve</span>
  <span id="freeText11049870338279970568" style="display:none">Books like this one are the reason why I read and love fantasy. N. K. Jemisin has a way of creating believable and exciting worlds that make me think about my own in a way that I haven't before. While the world in this series is (so far/ for me) not as impressive as the one created in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19161852.The_Fifth_Season__The_Broken_Earth___1_" title="The Fifth Season (The Broken Earth, #1) by N.K. Jemisin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fifth Season</a>, it is still highly original and a wonderful basis for the type of stories she excells in.<br /><br />Set in a world where after a war between the gods some of those gods are enslaved by humans and one is revered, the main character, Yeine, is thrust into a court full of intrigue and subtlety and hatred when her estranged grandfather names her his potential heir. We follow Yeine trying to survive long enough to stand a chance to become Queen. She needs to learn who to trust and who to avoid, but mostly she needs to learn who she wants to be and where her loyalties lie. <br /><br />My absolute favourite part were the characters Jemisin created - Yeine is a wonderful example of how to create a heroine who is kickass without being abrasive, strong-willed without being a caricature, flawed without being unsympathetic, and most of all fully believable and somebody I just rooted for since the very first page. I love the relationships she forges, both with the imprisoned gods and with other humans living in the palace, but mostly I loved her relationship with Sieh - a trickster god so great he reminded me of Shakespeare's Puck Robin. Sieh is such an amazing and different character and Jemisin never lets you forget that he isn't human.<br /><br />So, yes. I loved it a lot. And I cannot wait to read the next book in this trilogy and I am beyond excited to see where this story goes next. N. K. Jemisin is fast becoming one of my favourite authors.<br /><br />____<br />Having thought about this book some more, I have to give it five stars. Everything above still stands.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11049870338279970568" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_201341853" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/201341853" />
    <a title="Gergana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312798-gergana"><img alt="Gergana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1439319393p2/5312798.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312798-gergana?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
