        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer201341853" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17643683379512444143"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1484945485i/21770548._SY540_.png' width='300' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>First read in 2010 <br/>Last read in 2016</i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1484945485i/21770549._SX540_.png' width='250' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>All images are drawn by me, for higher resolution visit gerynh.tumblr.com</i><br/><br/>GODS! Yep, this series is about Gods.<br/><br/>100 000 Kingdoms was my first "what-the-hell-there-are-no-dragons-here-and-it's-not-Harry-Potter" type of book. It was the first novel that introduced me to fictional politics and quiet mysterious dudes with power over darkness... that turned out to be one of my many many weaknesses...<br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16096824.A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses__A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses___1_' title='A Court of Thorns and Roses (A Court of Thorns and Roses, #1) by Sarah J. Maas' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1491595796s/16096824.jpg' alt='A Court of Thorns and Roses (A Court of Thorns and Roses, #1) by Sarah J. Maas' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3227063.The_Way_of_Shadows__Night_Angel___1_' title='The Way of Shadows (Night Angel, #1) by Brent Weeks' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1327881551s/3227063.jpg' alt='The Way of Shadows (Night Angel, #1) by Brent Weeks' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/153219.Into_the_Dark_Lands__The_Sundered___1_' title='Into the Dark Lands (The Sundered, #1) by Michelle Sagara West' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1388214783s/153219.jpg' alt='Into the Dark Lands (The Sundered, #1) by Michelle Sagara West' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194157.Shadow_and_Bone__The_Grisha___1_' title='Shadow and Bone (The Grisha, #1) by Leigh Bardugo' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1339533695s/10194157.jpg' alt='Shadow and Bone (The Grisha, #1) by Leigh Bardugo' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>... damn you sexy shadow-wielding-men!<br/><br/><b>There are a f</b></span>
  <span id="freeText17643683379512444143" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1484945485i/21770548._SY540_.png" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>First read in 2010 <br>Last read in 2016</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1484945485i/21770549._SX540_.png" width="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>All images are drawn by me, for higher resolution visit gerynh.tumblr.com</i><br><br>GODS! Yep, this series is about Gods.<br><br>100 000 Kingdoms was my first "what-the-hell-there-are-no-dragons-here-and-it's-not-Harry-Potter" type of book. It was the first novel that introduced me to fictional politics and quiet mysterious dudes with power over darkness... that turned out to be one of my many many weaknesses...<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16096824.A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses__A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses___1_" title="A Court of Thorns and Roses (A Court of Thorns and Roses, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1491595796s/16096824.jpg" alt="A Court of Thorns and Roses (A Court of Thorns and Roses, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3227063.The_Way_of_Shadows__Night_Angel___1_" title="The Way of Shadows (Night Angel, #1) by Brent Weeks" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1327881551s/3227063.jpg" alt="The Way of Shadows (Night Angel, #1) by Brent Weeks" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/153219.Into_the_Dark_Lands__The_Sundered___1_" title="Into the Dark Lands (The Sundered, #1) by Michelle Sagara West" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1388214783s/153219.jpg" alt="Into the Dark Lands (The Sundered, #1) by Michelle Sagara West" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194157.Shadow_and_Bone__The_Grisha___1_" title="Shadow and Bone (The Grisha, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1339533695s/10194157.jpg" alt="Shadow and Bone (The Grisha, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>... damn you sexy shadow-wielding-men!<br><br><b>There are a few reasons why you might enjoy this book:</b><br>A. You're into mythology and legends, you like books about gods and their interactions with mortals.<br>B. You're into philosophy, contemplating what would happen if part of humanity had control over divine powers.<br>C. You would like to see another hot juicy romance between a simple mortal girl and a dude-controlling-shadows #437.<br>D. You like the cover! (Best reason of them all!)<br><br><b>~~~~~~~~~PLOT (Yeine's story)~~~~~~~~~~</b><br><br>Imagine a world of a hundred thousand kingdoms... And one kingdom to rule them all. Muahaha!<br><br>A kingdom that has actual Gods as slaves and the ruling family, the Arameri, can command them at will. This is the world of Yeine, a half-blooded Arameri and a leader of a small matriarchal tribe that is barely surviving in the jungles. One day she is summoned to the court of her grandfather, the King, in the city of Sky and named potential heir to the crown.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1484945485i/21770550._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Yeine</i> <br><br>Yeine comes from a tribe where women don't shy from battles and, as a leader, she isn't inexperienced in politics and back-stabbing. Yet, the whole situation doesn't make any sense to her: why is her grandfather interested in her now, after so many years. Why would he name her heir, when there are already two contestant competing for the crown. <br><br>When Yeine arrives at the palace it doesn't take long for her to get in trouble with other Arameri and the Gods themselves. Sure, having a mass of darkness (aka. Nahadoth, the God of darkness) chase you around a floating castle, isn't an ideal first day for anyone, but Yeine soon manages to establish alliances with the majority of the Gods inhabiting the place, promising them freedom in exchange for their aid to become the next successor to the crown.<br><br><b>~~~~~~~~~PLOT (The Gods' story)~~~~~~~~~~</b><br><br>In this world of a hundred thousand kingdoms there is peace (most of the time). Wars cause too much chaos and change, something that the main deity of this world - Itempas, despises. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1484945485i/21770551._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Itempas - God of law, order and light.</i><br><br>But it wasn't always like that.<br><br>Long ago, there were three main Gods. <br><br>Itempas - the god of law, order and light<br>Nahadoth - the god (and sometimes goddess) of darkness, night and chaos. <br>And Enefa - the goddess of twilight, dawn, life and death. <br><br>One day Itempas, guided by jealousy and loneliness, slew Enefa and imprisoned Nahadoth and three of the children gods, to serve humanity. (More details in book 2 which is actually even better XD)<br><br>Anyways, let's just say that most of the Arameri are kind of messed up in the head and even an ancient, all powerful and immortal being, such as the God of Darkness will do anything possible to "misinterpret" their commands and screw with them as much as possible. Nevertheless, it's not easy being a slave, being able to use your power only when you're commanded to and watching your children being tortured for centuries by the species you were part of creating.<br><br>&lt;<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1484945485i/21770552._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Nahadoth</i><br><br><b>~~~~What I liked~~~~</b><br><br><b>The World</b> - Sure, I can't say it was the most imaginative and complex fictional place I've ever been to, but it has its own charm. In terms of geography, it's nothing spectacular. The best part, of course, is the mythology and how the Gods fit into the whole story. It was interesting to see such powerful beings trapped into human existence, how people's mind can change when not even the majority of the Gods can oppose their will. Speaking of which...<br><br><b>The Gods</b> - They are massive, fathomless and incomprehensible. I loved it when they tried to act human for the benefit of Yeine (or when they were forced to by the Arameri), but then they would say or do something that will leave you feeling uneasy and shaky. Nahadoth is able to use only a fraction of his power during the night and you get a feeling that this book can only touch the surface of his character.<br><br><b>Sieh</b> - the God of childhood and lies, is probably my favorite character. He is the eldest of the godlings, yet, he appears (most of the time) as a nine-year old child - innocent, sweet and curious. Sieh is the first godling to befriend Yeine and he always tries to appeal to her motherly instincts. However even children are capable of cruelty and deceit. Sieh has planets and suns as his toys, he is capable of stealing away worlds and threatening to kill you in the most horrifying way. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1484945485i/21770553._SY540_.png" width="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>~~~~What I didn't like~~~~</b><br><br><b>Romance </b>- the romance between Yeine and Nahadoth didn't really resonate with me. It wasn't bad, but I missed the emotional connection between the characters. The whole time, it felt like they were just using eachother to achieve their goals. And I liked that. I prefer to see them as friends with benefits ;)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1484945485i/21770554._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Yiene </b>- I wasn't a huge fan of Yiene for some reason. She is supposed to be a strong and clever woman, but most of the time she spends running around and worrying about smaller things rather than looking at the whole picture. <br><br><b>~~~~The Final Verdict~~~~</b><br><br>A Hundred Thousand Kingdoms is a unique, thought-provoking and imaginative book with intriguing politics, complex characters and <s>sexy shadow-wielding-dudes</s> ahem...amazing world-building. It's in my list of favorites and there is nothing I would love to do more than push this book in people's faces until they agree to read it. Unfortunately, I'm not an Arameri and I don't own any Gods to punish anyone who opposes my will...<br><br><b>Would I recommend to a friend?</b>My answer is... it depends. Do you like political fantasy (not too overly complicated)? Do you want a read a book about immortal, all-powerful beings trapped into human existence? Are you fond of romance (that didn't make a lot of sense for me, but it was still good). Do you have hundreds and hundreds of books in your tbr-shelf and wouldn't mind adding one more? If the answer is "yes" then go ahead. I hope you enjoy it as much as I did (hopefully, even more) :) <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1484945485i/21770555._SY540_.png" width="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>More Recommendations:<br><br>Books with sexy shadow-wielding-men:<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16096824.A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses__A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses___1_" title="A Court of Thorns and Roses (A Court of Thorns and Roses, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1491595796s/16096824.jpg" alt="A Court of Thorns and Roses (A Court of Thorns and Roses, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3227063.The_Way_of_Shadows__Night_Angel___1_" title="The Way of Shadows (Night Angel, #1) by Brent Weeks" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1327881551s/3227063.jpg" alt="The Way of Shadows (Night Angel, #1) by Brent Weeks" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/153219.Into_the_Dark_Lands__The_Sundered___1_" title="Into the Dark Lands (The Sundered, #1) by Michelle Sagara West" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1388214783s/153219.jpg" alt="Into the Dark Lands (The Sundered, #1) by Michelle Sagara West" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194157.Shadow_and_Bone__The_Grisha___1_" title="Shadow and Bone (The Grisha, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1339533695s/10194157.jpg" alt="Shadow and Bone (The Grisha, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Shadow and Bone by Leigh Bardugo is my favorite, A Court of Thorns and Roses is pretty popular too. Both are YA though, and focus more on the romance (which I didn't get, yet again).<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9461562.The_Cloud_Roads__Books_of_the_Raksura___1_" title="The Cloud Roads (Books of the Raksura, #1) by Martha Wells" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1317017378s/9461562.jpg" alt="The Cloud Roads (Books of the Raksura, #1) by Martha Wells" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Cloud Roads by Martha Wells - a book that was recommended by N.K. Jemisin and ended up becoming one of my top 5 favorites! It's unique and freaking amazing!</span>

<div id="review_1686275937" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1686275937" />
    <a title="Matthew Quann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22699228-matthew-quann"><img alt="Matthew Quann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528393487p2/22699228.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1686275937?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew Quann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew Quann" href="/user/show/22699228-matthew-quann">Matthew Quann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fantasy fans, adventure-seekers, change of pace</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22699228-matthew-quann?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1686275937" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5254333008509198542">Man, oh man, oh man, oh man...this book was <b>PHENOMENAL.</b><br/><br/>I honestly can't remember the last book that kept me so fastened to the couch, ignoring social calls and daily rituals just to read one more chapter. Okay, maybe just one more...you get the picture. This book is relentlessly fun, and for a first novel in a trilogy it moves at an unrelenting clip. I kept saying that I'd put the book down, only for the end of a chapter to beg a bit more reading. This book gave me a much needed defibrillation t</span>
  <span id="freeText5254333008509198542" style="display:none">Man, oh man, oh man, oh man...this book was <b>PHENOMENAL.</b><br /><br />I honestly can't remember the last book that kept me so fastened to the couch, ignoring social calls and daily rituals just to read one more chapter. Okay, maybe just one more...you get the picture. This book is relentlessly fun, and for a first novel in a trilogy it moves at an unrelenting clip. I kept saying that I'd put the book down, only for the end of a chapter to beg a bit more reading. This book gave me a much needed defibrillation to my summer reading that has left me invigorated. <br /><br />The worst part? The trilogy collection sat on my shelf for months and months, always put off in place of a novel I thought might be more "important", challenging, or rewarding. I originally decided to pick up the trilogy for two reasons:<br /><br /><b>a)</b>Junot Diaz (a favourite author of mine) placed it on his world-building creative writing syllabus at MIT. A syllabus which highlights a diverse group of authors rather than just a bunch of white dudes. Check out that syllabus <a href="http://www.openculture.com/2015/02/junot-diazs-syllabi-for-his-mit-writing-classes.html" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a><br /><br /><b>b)</b>I got the entire trilogy omnibus for $13 or $15, which is a real steal for such a hyped fantasy author. <br /><br />But, as I mentioned, I kept putting the whole series off. Then, as I was finishing up with my last couple books, I decided to put my intended reading list on hold and test the waters with Jemisin's trilogy. If nothing else, I was sure that it would be a reprieve from the heavier stuff I've been into lately. <br /><br />As you may have already gathered, I couldn't get enough.<br /><br /><b>Our story</b> begins with a style that instantly caught me off-guard for a fantasy novel. First person narrative, sure. But the modern dialect and style? The asides directed (seemingly) at the audience? This book, right away, declared itself different from the pack. Yeine, a barbarian girl called from her country to live amongst her mother's royal family, gets to hang out with the gods. The rub is this: thousands of years ago there was a calamity and the gods were enslaved by Yeine's ancestors. Of course, there's a good bit of slavery going on with the general population in Sky, the city built for royals by their enslaved gods.<br /><br />Jemisin does something really great here: she makes a story about the myriad horrors of slavery using a really awesome fantasy narrative. As I was ripping through pages and Jemisin was battering down fantasy tropes, I had to pause every once and a while to admire the different type of story she was trying to tell. This book isn't all about sword fights, magic battles, and struggles for power (though there's that too). There's sex, thoughtful conversation, and a heroine whose strength demands to be admired. I was pleasantly surprised by Jemisin's ability to take what I worried would be a tired romance story and turn it into a series of cosmic, universe-bending sex scenes. It may sound crude, but Jemisin elevates the genre by touching on subjects and concepts that other authors shy away from, sex being just one of them.<br /><br />Of course, this is all stuff I love. I loved fantasy novels when I was growing up and I usually can take something from even the bad ones I read today. I mean, there's just something appealing about a dragon fight that doesn't need a lot of dressing up. But I can understand that not everybody has that same sense of nostalgia and affinity for a given genre. What makes <i>The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms</i> so great is that it refuses to play by the rules and tropes of fantasy, and instead offers a new type of narrative that feels important. The lore is unique, the writing modern and exciting, the characters vividly imagined (Nahadoth and Sieh stole entire scenes for me), and Jemisin's traded a pseudo-medieval Europe setting for something completely different. <br /><br />So, I totally recommend this one. I haven't had this much fun with a book all year. I loved uncovering the secrets of Yeine's family drama, I absorbed the history of the gods, and thoroughly enjoyed the Hogwarts-as-torture-castle setting of Sky. The story also ends in a way that sated my hunger for the story and characters but also, in a cute bit of narration, promises more to come. So, you could read this one and move on, but with such a cheap omnibus, why not keep on with it? I'll be reading the rest of the trilogy over the summer, using them as breaks between some of the more obtuse writing I have ahead of me. <br /><br />But enough time spent with me and my review. <br /><br />You've all got a book to read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5254333008509198542" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2193843106" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2193843106" />
    <a title="Charlotte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11475773-charlotte"><img alt="Charlotte" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487528389p2/11475773.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2193843106?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte" href="/user/show/11475773-charlotte">Charlotte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2193843106&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2193843106" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15397059439085568475"><i>"It is blasphemy to separate oneself from the earth and look down on it like a god. It is more than blasphemy; it is dangerous. We can never be gods, after all—but we can become something less than human with frightening ease."</i><br/><br/>It's been a bit since my last review- welcome back. Today I'm talking about N.K. Jemisin's The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms, published in 2010. Spoilers follow!<br/><br/><b>So What's It About?</b><br/><br/>Yeine Darr is summoned to the magnificent floating city of Sky by her grandfather, the ruler of t</span>
  <span id="freeText15397059439085568475" style="display:none"><i>"It is blasphemy to separate oneself from the earth and look down on it like a god. It is more than blasphemy; it is dangerous. We can never be gods, after all—but we can become something less than human with frightening ease."</i><br /><br />It's been a bit since my last review- welcome back. Today I'm talking about N.K. Jemisin's The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms, published in 2010. Spoilers follow!<br /><br /><b>So What's It About?</b><br /><br />Yeine Darr is summoned to the magnificent floating city of Sky by her grandfather, the ruler of the known world. To her shock, he names her as one of his heirs, a naming that is virtually a death sentence given the bloodthirsty nature of Arameri politics. As she struggles for her life, she comes to realize that there are even more powers at work in Sky than she had ever reckoned, and to uncover the truth of her family's secrets and keep her life she must turn to the ancient gods that are enslaved in the palace. But the gods have their own plans...<br /><br /><b>What I Thought</b><br /><br />There is something so fundamentally addictive and compelling about the way N.K. Jemisin writes. She is so deft and bold, with a perfectly-honed sense of when to drop a tantalizing hint or a stunning reveal and such a gripping way of weaving a net of story-telling around her characters.<br /><br />A friend told me that as soon as she finished this book, she immediately turned back to the first page and started it over again. I have to say that I was strongly tempted to do the same after the final puzzle pieces slid into place and I finally grasped the magnitude of what was happening. Isn't it such a wonderful moment when you finally understand a story in all of its complexity after the last secret has been revealed? There were so many clever hints and nods at the truth along the way, but while they kept me eager to puzzle it all out, I felt they they were opaque enough to keep me from figuring it out too early.<br /><br />The gods and goddesses that are at the heart of The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms are a fascinating bunch in their paradoxes - unknowably powerful yet enslaved by the Arameri; creators and shapers of mankind yet reviled and abused by their creations; sometimes disarmingly mundane in their appearances and interactions, at other times completely alien and ancient. Sieh the Trickster and Nahadoth the Nightlord are the two gods that Yeine comes to know the best during her time in Sky, and they both have many faces.<br /><br />Sieh takes the form of an affectionate, playful child yet is the oldest godling, billions of years old and capricious in his motivations and dangerous in his own right. Nahadoth is, by his essence, shaped in reaction to those who surround him- and shaped by the cruel world of the Arameri he is chaos, death and seduction embodied.<br /><br /><i>“When I am free,” he said, “I will choose who shapes me.”</i><br /><br />Yeine's fascination with him is nearly inevitable, given his nature, but what sets her apart from the rest of Sky is that she acknowledges his current lack of agency and its wrongness by essentially deciding to make herself powerless before him in return - and it is upon those equalizing grounds that she will sleep with him, and no other. It turns out that sex with an eons-old god is something of a metaphysical trip, actually:<br /><br /><i>"...past endless stars, past countless worlds, through layers of light and glowing cloud. Up and up we went, our speed impossible, our size incomprehensible. We left the light behind and kept going, passing through stranger things than mere worlds. Geometric shapes that twisted and gibbered. A white landscape of frozen explosions. Shivering lines of intention that turned to chase us. Vast, whalelike beings with terrifying eyes and the faces of long-lost friends."</i><br /><br />I have to admit that the story's ending was much more hopeful than I had expected. There was so much cruelty, so many instances of Sky's callousness and cynicism at play, such proof of the gods' merciless power that I really had no idea how Yeine could possibly find anything at the end of her journey other than death. Ascension to godhood is not the typical grounds for a happily-ever-after, but it did truly feel like the perfect way for the story to end. I also appreciated that there were still people who clung to their goodness amongst all the cruelty that Sky had to offer;I have high hopes for T'vril's leadership abilities despite the significant challenges he will face, and I appreciated that Relad eventually decided to do the right thing and help Yeine.<br /><br /><b>The F Word</b><br /><br />The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms is often deeply concerned with questions of agency, free will, consent and power. From what her mother did to Yeine to the way that the gods remain trapped in slavery by their own brother and the deep societal divides and injustices that exist because of the Arameri dynasty and their violent colonialist legacy, this book spends a great deal of time reflecting on power is abused, how the ability to choose can be exploited and removed, and what happens once it does.<br /><br />Yeine's home country of Darr is a matriarchal society of people of color, and she leads them and protects them through her self-possession, determination and competence. Yeine is in many ways a very emotionally-reserved character, and I really appreciated the moments where she was able to show her vulnerability and express her struggle with the fate that was written for her. I think oftentimes black female characters are expected to be endless wells of strength in the face of suffering, and with that in mind I'm really glad that Jemisin depicted Yeine as a fallible character who, despite her power and competence, still needed support and comfort from others given what she was facing.<br /><br />And, as a final point, I'd be remiss if I didn't mention a certain line in the Acknowledgements at the end of the book:<br /><br /><i>"Posthumous thanks to Octavia Butler, for going first and showing the rest of us how it’s done."</i><br /><br /><b>About the Author</b><br /><br />Nora K. Jemisin was born in Iowa City in 1972, and studied psychology at Tulane University. After obtaining her Masters, she worked as a therapist before becoming a writer full time. The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms was her debut novel, published in 2010, and it went on to win the Sense of Gender Award and the Locus Award for Best First Novel. She was the first black woman to win the Hugo Award for best novel for The Fifth Season, and went on to break more ground by winning the Hugo again in the following two years for the next books in the Broken Earth trilogy. She is an outspoken advocate against racism and sexism within the SFF community, and lives in New York.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15397059439085568475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2193843106">

<div id="review_635064347" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/635064347" />
    <a title="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship"><img alt="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325201543p2/5229326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/635064347?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" href="/user/show/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship">Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer635064347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2726733775330359819">This book had a lot of hype when it was first released, followed by a backlash that seemed primarily motivated by the fact there is romance in it. Now that I’ve gotten around to reading this, I did not enjoy it, but that had less to do with the fact that the protagonist hooks up with a dark god than that the story just isn’t very interesting.<br/> <br/>Yeine is a young woman who travels to a distant land and gets caught up in court politics over her head – standard fantasy stuff. The story is told through</span>
  <span id="freeText2726733775330359819" style="display:none">This book had a lot of hype when it was first released, followed by a backlash that seemed primarily motivated by the fact there is romance in it. Now that I’ve gotten around to reading this, I did not enjoy it, but that had less to do with the fact that the protagonist hooks up with a dark god than that the story just isn’t very interesting.<br /> <br />Yeine is a young woman who travels to a distant land and gets caught up in court politics over her head – standard fantasy stuff. The story is told through Yeine’s first-person narration, looking back on events, and her voice is the one aspect of the book I sort of liked. On the one hand, it is strong and assured, and the digressions and circling back to add new information and asides to the reader give the sense of a person actually telling a story. On the other hand, this voice – reflective, detached, polished – clearly belongs to a writer, while our 19-year-old Yeine is supposed to be the warrior queen of a female-dominated barbarian tribe.<br /> <br />I say “supposed to be” not only because she doesn’t sound anything like that, but also because she doesn’t act like it. In her actions she is astoundingly passive, a Generic Female Protagonist used as a pawn by everyone around her, who spends most of the book waiting for events others have set in motion. Such passivity not only leaches interest from the story, but prevents me from even classifying it as epic fantasy. The defining characteristic of that subgenre is a struggle between good and evil. There’s evil here, thanks to the gratuitous acts of brutality that are apparently required in all fantasy novels in the Game of Thrones era (I say this as someone who loves the Song of Ice and Fire series, but could do without the often out-of-place attempts at grittiness in every other fantasy novel). But there’s no struggle. Yeine doesn't try to fight back. She's an object of others' actions, lacking goals of her own; she quickly gives up even on the modest aspiration of surviving her royal family’s backstabbing, hoping only to accomplish with her death an act suggested to her for their own benefit by some characters she’s just met, who have then agreed to assist her people, who are never even introduced. Now tell me that sounds like a rousing plot.<br /> <br />Other than Yeine, there are fewer than a dozen characters in the book, most of whom are plot devices with at best one character trait. And although there are supposedly a hundred thousand kingdoms, all the action takes place in the bland, white imperial city of Sky. Jemisin develops the world’s mythology, but not its present; there’s no sense of life in it. Back to poor Yeine: she’s supposed to have come from a matriarchal society in which the government and army are all female, but upon arriving in Sky, where almost everyone in power is male, has no reaction to or comment on this difference. An easy mistake to make in a setting lacking sufficient culture for anyone to be a convincing product of it.<br /> <br />Yes, you can find fantasy much worse than this, but I found nothing here to hold my attention: not the plot, not the characters, not the world. I’m glad other readers enjoy Jemisin’s work, but after reading a book and a half (the half was The Killing Moon, which I finally set aside because while technically better than this one, it had not inspired even minimal interest), I have to conclude that it is not for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2726733775330359819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_130436962" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/130436962" />
    <a title="Janina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3455554-janina"><img alt="Janina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404584313p2/3455554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/130436962?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Janina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Janina" href="/user/show/3455554-janina">Janina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781841498171" href="/book/show/6612542-the-hundred-thousand-kingdoms">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer130436962" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10330725731763413130">What did I expect from <b>The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms</b>? Honestly, I can’t tell. When I saw the translation of book two in a German bookstore some weeks ago, I simply was drawn in by the blurb on the back of the book. It sounded like a stand-alone – or at least like the first book in a trilogy – so when I went looking for the English version, I was surprised to find out that it was in fact not. Now, the summary of book one didn’t sound as intriguing to me at all, but I figured I would maybe not be </span>
  <span id="freeText10330725731763413130" style="display:none">What did I expect from <b>The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms</b>? Honestly, I can’t tell. When I saw the translation of book two in a German bookstore some weeks ago, I simply was drawn in by the blurb on the back of the book. It sounded like a stand-alone – or at least like the first book in a trilogy – so when I went looking for the English version, I was surprised to find out that it was in fact not. Now, the summary of book one didn’t sound as intriguing to me at all, but I figured I would maybe not be able to enjoy the second instalment in its entirety if I didn’t read it. Let me tell you, the summary does not do this novel justice. It makes it sound pretty average in the field of epic fantasy:<br /><br />Parent dies under mysterious circumstances? Check.<br />Heroine is thrust into a completely new and unfamiliar situation? Check.<br />Heroine is presented with a seemingly impossible challenge? Check.<br />You don’t know who is to be trusted and who plays fair? Check.<br />And, most importantly, the summary includes the words <i>political intrigue</i> or <i>power struggles</i>? Check.<br /><br />But <b>The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms</b> is anything but average. It is fresh and original, and surprisingly different. I really don’t want to say too much about the actual plot because I think it’s best to go into this book not really knowing what to expect. I have to admit that some concepts were a bit difficult for me to grasp, to relate to entirely, but nevertheless, I enjoyed this book immensely.<br /><br />A special trait surely is the narration. The book is told in first person, as a kind of giant flashback with shifts in time every now and then. The style is somehow informal, with Yeine, the main character, addressing the reader directly from time to time. There are hints at what will happen later, dreams and conversation with unknown people thrown in where they don't seem to fit, flashbacks to events some days previous. So yes, I think you can kind of get an idea of what happens in the end, but for me those passages were a little too cryptic to figure out. They are clearly distracting and might leave you more than a little confused – but I think they are meant to be that way.<br /><br />Even though the full potential is not <i>always</i> realized, this novel is amazingly carved out in both characterisation and world building for a debut. It clearly differs from the <i>We-are-on-an-important-quest-to-rescue-mankind-so-let’s-be-solemn-and-stern</i> kind of books to be found in the genre. It represents more an inner struggle than an epic war fought out on the battlefield, but for me that was just right. I tend to get bored by battles pretty quickly. Also, you won’t find any characters here that are <i>only</i> good or <i>only</i> bad. Mostly, they are refreshingly ambivalent.<br /><br />Recommended for everyone looking for a different kind of fantasy who is not weirded out by the idea of gods and mortals mingling – in every possible sense ;).<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10330725731763413130" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_137623603" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137623603" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597876967p2/1343864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137623603?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=sexytimes">sexytimes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=romantical">romantical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=class-gender-race">class-gender-race</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=speculative">speculative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=murder-most-foul">murder-most-foul</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=award-winners">award-winners</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=folklore-and-mythology">folklore-and-mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=not-quite-five-stars-but-sooo-close">not-quite-five-stars-but-sooo-close</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137623603" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer805331898611039240">You can always tell when you come across something and know you've never quite read anything like it before, because afterwards, your brain won't know quite how to file it away. It has to create new paradigms to fit stuff into. I was in that stage for quite a while after reading this weird, sensual, dark, joyful book.<br/><br/>Our main character Yeine lives in a world where belief in the gods is not an option. The gods walk among them. It's a world where one nation, the Arameri, have all the power because</span>
  <span id="freeText805331898611039240" style="display:none">You can always tell when you come across something and know you've never quite read anything like it before, because afterwards, your brain won't know quite how to file it away. It has to create new paradigms to fit stuff into. I was in that stage for quite a while after reading this weird, sensual, dark, joyful book.<br /><br />Our main character Yeine lives in a world where belief in the gods is not an option. The gods walk among them. It's a world where one nation, the Arameri, have all the power because 2,000 years before when the God's War sundered their world, they landed on the winning side. There are many gods and godlings, but only three main gods. The winning god, Itempas, killed his sister, who had betrayed him, and now imprisons his brother and the children who fought on their side. It is this that makes the Arameri powerful. Itempas gave them the defeated gods in human form, imprisoning them at the will of the Arameri. For 2,000 years they are used as playthings and world-destroying weapons. <br /><br />Yeine's mother was Arameri, but was exiled when she married Yeine's father, a man from a "barbarian" culture. But now Yeine's mother has died under mysterious circumstances, and she has suddenly been made heir to her grandfather, the leader of the Arameri. Yeine is thrust into a fraught situation with very little knowledge, and has to play power games and figure out the complicated mysteries of the Arameri and their godling playthings in order to survive.<br /><br />The whole thing turns into this mystical, surprisingly sexy, twisted journey of spirituality and power, and it was soooo hard to put down. It was also really weird, and in parts, I had to keep reminding myself it was fiction so my brain would calm down. <br /><br />Jemisin has a beautiful way with words, and the characters she creates feel very real. She also peoples her worlds with diverse cultures and races of people, and her world is one of fluid and surprising sexuality. If you're a fantasy fan and you haven't tried this series yet, I highly highly recommend that you do. It's epic in a way I've never seen fantasy be epic before. I am definitely a fan of this author now (especially after reading the second book in the series, which was my favorite).</span>
  <a data-text-id="805331898611039240" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_794900892" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/794900892" />
    <a title="Lazaros" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22313662-lazaros"><img alt="Lazaros" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578697302p2/22313662.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/794900892?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lazaros" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lazaros" href="/user/show/22313662-lazaros">Lazaros</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">epic/high fantasy lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer794900892" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3782199995679158609"><b>
  <blockquote>“We can never be gods, after all - but we can become something less than human with frightening ease.”</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/>Such a pleasant, pleasant surprise. I loved this so much.<br/><br/>There may be some <b>minor spoilers in this</b>, so, go ahead & read at your own volition. No big, spoily spoilers, though! Just explaining things a little.<br/><br/>I'm not sure where to begin. Should I may begin by how much well-written this was? N. K. Jemisin is one hell of an author, that is most certain. It was detailed without being tiring, it ha</span>
  <span id="freeText3782199995679158609" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>“We can never be gods, after all - but we can become something less than human with frightening ease.”</blockquote>
</b><br /><br />Such a pleasant, pleasant surprise. I loved this so much.<br /><br />There may be some <b>minor spoilers in this</b>, so, go ahead &amp; read at your own volition. No big, spoily spoilers, though! Just explaining things a little.<br /><br />I'm not sure where to begin. Should I may begin by how much well-written this was? N. K. Jemisin is one hell of an author, that is most certain. It was detailed without being tiring, it had many characters &amp; each of them was well-made. I loved the world, it was nicely-crafted. The history was breathtaking &amp; I loved every part of it. From Godswar to how it all came down to the Enefadeh being prisoners of the Arameri.<br /><br />Yeine Darr is an Arameri. Her mother was one &amp; she's one by inheritance. She's called to the 'Sky' (a floating palace, that's a sight to build in your head) by her grandfather who's, in a way, the King though the Hundred Thousand Kingdoms are not ruled by just one person. There we'll see what a nice person her grandfather is &amp; I'm sure you'll all despise him. Yeine is one of the three contenders for her grandfather's position. Two cousins of her are also in the run. The problem is that she is in danger, from the moment her grandfather got her in the competition. Her cousins are dangerous &amp; will stop at nothing to destroy - kill - her.<br /><br />In her first day at the palace she meets the Gods. Let's go back a minute. It all stars when the God of Light, the Bright Itempas, killed Enefa, the Goddess of Twilight &amp; Dawn &amp; punished his brother, the Nightlord, Nahadoth &amp; all the lesser Gods by confining them in human bodies. Let's just say that all the Gods, except for Bright Itempas, are bound to do whatever the Arameri want &amp; must obey them at all costs. Scimina, Yeine's cousin, unleashes Nahadoth, one of the Three &amp; the firs to be created for he is the very embodiment of darkness &amp; chaos, &amp; another God, Sieh saves her. Sieh is the God of Mischief. <br /><br />Yeine, at first, isn't even aware of who they are but when the feeling sinks in &amp; they make her an offer she has to decide whether she should side with those who are prisoned or those who want to kill her. Though, the decision is easy to make she must not be quick to do so because she really doesn't know why the Enefadeh want to assist her.<br /><br />I won't delve more into this. I'll just say that Yeine is an amazing character &amp; I loved her thoughts &amp; I loved being inside her head &amp; I loved the relationship she built with all of the Enefadeh, how she loved them &amp; found friends &amp; lovers in them. The romance was not a usual one, it was unusual, it was all about attraction &amp; lust at first &amp; it felt kind of weird but then I grew accustomed to it &amp; the romance showed itself. <br /><br />From the Gods, I must say I loved Nahadoth the most. He was just so mysterious, he had so many aspects. He has lost all of his compassion towards any human and he's vulgar &amp; hard at first &amp; it's difficult to understand him. He's all kinds of fucked-up &amp; there's so much to him. Including how at night, when the sun goes down, he goes into full kickass mode &amp; loses every bit of humanity he has during the day. It's nice to see how Yeine gets through to him. Also, Sieh, that little boy-man, may be the cutest thing ever. He always wanted to hug &amp; cuddle &amp; he developed the most beautiful friendship with Yeine.<br /><br />The ending was satisfying &amp; I can't wait to get into the second book &amp; read more of this amazing, broken world &amp; the characters. <br /><br />Don't be doubtful about reading this. Just grab &amp; read it, I'm sure you'll relish this. <br /><br />Thanks for reading my review, bookworms. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="3782199995679158609" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3593866900" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3593866900" />
    <a title="Sofia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/114413220-sofia"><img alt="Sofia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606141536p2/114413220.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3593866900?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sofia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sofia" href="/user/show/114413220-sofia">Sofia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=disappointments">disappointments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=lost-interest">lost-interest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=mary-sue">mary-sue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=what-just-happened">what-just-happened</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=well-that-was-a-cheap-plot">well-that-was-a-cheap-plot</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3593866900" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1007578533041866185">*yawn* Booooooriiiiing.<br/><br/>Maybe I have a short attention span (true) or I'm just not that into epic fantasy anymore (also true), but this was so unbearably slow that I nearly put it down three times before finally deciding to banish it to the DNF zone. <br/><br/>I've heard wonderful things about N.K. Jemisin, but this style of narration didn't really suit the mood. In the middle of an intense action scene, we would be pulled away for a history lesson on the culture and religion of Sky. And while I liked this</span>
  <span id="freeText1007578533041866185" style="display:none">*yawn* Booooooriiiiing.<br /><br />Maybe I have a short attention span (true) or I'm just not that into epic fantasy anymore (also true), but this was so unbearably slow that I nearly put it down three times before finally deciding to banish it to the DNF zone. <br /><br />I've heard wonderful things about N.K. Jemisin, but this style of narration didn't really suit the mood. In the middle of an intense action scene, we would be pulled away for a history lesson on the culture and religion of Sky. And while I liked this at first, it got old fast. Imagine if I wrote my reviews like this: <br /><br /><i>I've heard wonderful things about N.K. Jemisin, but this style of narration didn't really suit the mood. But I'm getting ahead of myself. <br /><br />* * *<br />This book was written in 2010. <br /><br />***<br />Ah, yes. Where was I?<br />In the middle of an intense action scene, we would be pulled away for a history lesson on the culture and religion of Sky.</i><br /><br />And so on and so forth. While it definitely was unique, it didn't fit the storyline as a whole, and made it rather disjointed. I also felt detached from the narrative somehow, as if I were watching this from the sky (hehe, puns) and seeing the action, rather than feeling it and being in the midst of it. <br /><br />This was honestly a really confusing book. Despite the strange narration, I thought I had a solid grip on the religion and customs of this floating city - until I tried to think of a way to recap the story... and failed. There are some gods who look like humans, and Yeine is competing to be the heir of a hotshot rich guy. That's all I remembered. And I stopped reading just a few hours ago. <br /><br />I was really disappointed by this, because it's N.K. Jemisin, and isn't she supposed to be the master of fantasy? On the surface, <i>The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms</i> seems like a book I would love. But it was soooo boring and slow, lacking compelling, original characters to keep me anchored. It wasn't very long till I was skimming. I decided I could spend my time on better books than this. <br /><br />DNF<br />1.5 stars</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_77244175" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/77244175" />
    <a title="new_user" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1365355-new-user"><img alt="new_user" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351189841p2/1365355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/77244175?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="new_user" class="user" itemprop="url" name="new_user" href="/user/show/1365355-new-user">new_user</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1365355-new-user?shelf=racially-diverse">racially-diverse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1365355-new-user?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer77244175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13794731323801684909"><b>N.K. Jemisin approaches empire in her epic fantasy debut, <i>The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms</i>.</b> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/88609.Laura_Resnick' title='Laura Resnick' rel='nofollow noopener'>Laura Resnick</a> (<i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1425672.In_Legend_Born__Chronicles_of_Sirkara___1_' title='In Legend Born (Chronicles of Sirkara, #1) by Laura Resnick' rel='nofollow noopener'>In Legend Born</a>
</i>) conceived of conquered Silerians, but few authors discuss the national, political and local effects of imperialism, fearing bored readers and infodumps. Jemisin's subtlety indicates a social awareness, an appreciation for PR vs. reality, biased histories, and mistrust of power.<blockquote>"Once, like High North, Senm was also a land of barbarians, and the Amn were simply the most succe</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText13794731323801684909" style="display:none"><b>N.K. Jemisin approaches empire in her epic fantasy debut, <i>The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms</i>.</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/88609.Laura_Resnick" title="Laura Resnick" rel="nofollow noopener">Laura Resnick</a> (<i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1425672.In_Legend_Born__Chronicles_of_Sirkara___1_" title="In Legend Born (Chronicles of Sirkara, #1) by Laura Resnick" rel="nofollow noopener">In Legend Born</a>
</i>) conceived of conquered Silerians, but few authors discuss the national, political and local effects of imperialism, fearing bored readers and infodumps. Jemisin's subtlety indicates a social awareness, an appreciation for PR vs. reality, biased histories, and mistrust of power.<blockquote>"Once, like High North, Senm was also a land of barbarians, and the Amn were simply the most successful of these. After the war they imposed their barbarian ways on the whole world and judged the rest of us by how thoroughly we adopted them...</blockquote>Amn now rule the world. I'd have enjoyed more focus on these barbarians, many years later, advertising themselves as civilized and superior and inflicting their values on the 100,000 kingdoms. Instead, first-person <i>Kingdoms</i> follows Yeine, reluctant heir to the throne, in palace Sky for two weeks, and sometimes romance overwhelms the rest, but so does cutthroat intrigue-- and I'm okay with that.<br /><br />Yeine leads Darre, an Amazonian kingdom. She's no stranger to harsh, pragmatic politics, but Sky's schemes are another animal. Yeine's aim? Nothing so simplistic as overthrowing "evil" rulers. She's trying to stay alive. However, while assassination is not unheard of in Jemisin's realistic world, her Amn fight more subtly, surreal in their cruelty. Some readers may have trouble connecting to a tale populated by only gray characters. No one's the white knight, even Yeine.<br /><br />I enjoyed Yeine's intrigues and the mystery of Sky's history, Jemisin's characterizations, <i>Kingdoms'</i> mythos, but I wasn't convinced of Yeine's romance with a god. Something unequal there?<br /><br />By turns compassionate, sexay, alien or wrathful, god of night Nahadoth's always angsty. LOL, JK. (Remember Bishop's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47956.Daughter_of_the_Blood__The_Black_Jewels___1_" title="Daughter of the Blood (The Black Jewels, #1) by Anne Bishop" rel="nofollow noopener">Black Jewels</a>? Oh, his pain! His pain! Don't you feel his <i>pain?</i> Also similar: the primacy of female characters. It's only obvious in Darre, but Jemisin's male characters are all passive.) He's cool. My friend Ariana compares him to Neil Gaiman's <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_Dfhy6gn6epo/SxascCH5g9I/AAAAAAAAAAs/dNNJ5Yg7Vl4/s320/sandman-morpheus.jpg" target="new" rel="nofollow noopener">Morpheus</a> character from the <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23754.Preludes_and_Nocturnes__The_Sandman___1_" title="Preludes and Nocturnes (The Sandman, #1) by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">Sandman</a>
</i> comics with shadows curling from his black hair and cloak. <br /><br />Also, 5000 pts. for a non-white heroine and a non-Eurocentric setting. Jemisin's fictional patchwork of nations speaks to an East Asian influence of Jemisin-invented cultures and gods -two gods plus kids, with their meddling, jealousies and balance of power. <br /><br />Readers will like the misunderstood villain/bad boy/underdog, and I liked the theme of popular beliefs vs. reality, but the romance subplot took precedence too much for me. That said, I can't resist a blind hero or heroine, so I'll have to read <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7904453.The_Broken_Kingdoms__The_Inheritance_Trilogy___2_" title="The Broken Kingdoms (The Inheritance Trilogy, #2) by N.K. Jemisin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Broken Kingdoms</a>
</i>! <i>Kingdoms</i> can be read as a standalone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13794731323801684909" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('u1ezb/1aIwQ23V/r5AcPG60Qk5a+KprR5RA9SJJ50Ay9dJAeKXYi/7cgAoyoH177zw8+tv3Su4dcP0XzUBl+KQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('y+8H3SkWZXDdqu+QmSSK1BIZCQ5uFPy74tfP2jsX6l/NzCSs/Tpki1xXsvfVPNs0cAakLi3s3e1b+Ldh+XdEeg==')})
  }

To vanquish them, he must face some ugly truths about his history and put himself at the mercy of those he once considered enemies.\n\nHaving narrowly escaped their murderous families and Daevabad’s deadly politics, Nahri and Ali, now safe in Cairo, face difficult choices of their own. While Nahri finds peace in the old rhythms and familiar comforts of her human home, she is haunted by the knowledge that the loved ones she left behind and the people who considered her a savior are at the mercy of a new tyrant.
